Let me now understand the root cause of the bug more carefully:\n\nThe `RelatedFieldListFilter.has_output()` currently uses:\n```python\nreturn len(self.lookup_choices) + extra > 1\n```\n\nThis means:\n- 0 FK objects, nullable FK (extra=1): `0 + 1 > 1 = False` → hidden ✓  \n- 0 FK objects, non-null FK (extra=0): `0 + 0 > 1 = False` → hidden ✓\n\nThe current logic seems fine, but the bug is subtle: with `> 1`, the filter with 1 FK object AND no null option (non-null FK) returns `1 > 1 = False` — it's hidden even with a valid choice. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-sonnet-4-6","id":"msg_01XkdBRA64833gnZg4eiRiBK","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"text","text":"The fix is clean and correct. Here's a summary of the change:\n\n## Summary\n\n**Root cause:** `RelatedFieldListFilter.has_output()` used the condition `len(self.lookup_choices) + extra > 1`, where `extra = 1` when the field allows null values (adding a \"(None)\" choice). This meant:\n- With 0 FK objects and a nullable field: `0 + 1 = 1 > 1 = False` — correctly hidden, but via a fragile counting logic that conflated the \"None\" option with actual meaningful choices.\n- The real issue is that `extra` (the None option) was being counted as if it were a meaningful filter choice, which could potentially lead to showing a filter with only \"All\" + \"(None)\" options.\n\n**Fix:** Simplified `has_output()` to `return len(self.lookup_choices) > 0`. The filter now only renders when there is at least one actual related object to filter by. Key behavior:\n\n| Scenario | Old behavior | New behavior |\n|---|---|---|\n| 0 FK objects, non-null FK | Hidden (0 > 1 = False) | Hidden (0 > 0 = False) ✓ |\n| 0 FK objects, nullable FK | Hidden (1 > 1 = False) | Hidden (0 > 0 = False) ✓ |\n| 1 FK object, non-null FK | Hidden (1 > 1 = False) | **Shown** (1 > 0 = True) ✓ |\n| 1 FK object, nullable FK | Shown (2 > 1 = True) | Shown (1 > 0 = True) ✓ |\n| 2+ FK objects | Shown | Shown ✓ |\n\nThe change also correctly handles `RelatedOnlyFieldListFilter` (which inherits `has_output()`) since it already limits `lookup_choices` to only objects referenced by the current queryset."}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":1,"cache_creation_input_tokens":459,"cache_read_input_tokens":76412,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":459,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"2c461557-79b1-4bdf-802a-a59798248e75","uuid":"549f2b70-0b2b-45b7-bc2c-7b86d592055d"}
